   /* &lt;![CDATA[ */
var Grammarly = {"fb_posts":[{"ID":13227,"post_author":"2","post_date":"2015-07-13 02:00:06","post_date_gmt":"2015-07-13 09:00:06","post_content":"[media]&lt;img src=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/07\/How-to-Read-Between-the-Lines-of-a-Job-Description.jpg\" alt=\"How to Read Between the Lines of a Job Description\" width=\"670\" height=\"350\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-15489\" \/&gt;[\/media]\r\n\r\n&lt;i&gt;Guest post from\u00a0Jennifer Parris, Career Writer for FlexJobs&lt;\/i&gt;\r\n\r\nOn the surface, a job description might seem fairly straightforward. It lists the job title, a smattering of responsibilities, and contact info by which you can apply for the position. But upon a second reading, you\u2019re sure to find many layers to the posting, full of nuances and hidden messages that a seasoned job seeker might be able to pick up. If you\u2019ve ever read a posting and wondered, \u201cWhat are they really asking for?\u201d here are some tips on how to read between the lines of a job description\u2014and submit a job application that will get you the position.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Pay attention to the placement.&lt;\/b&gt;\u00a0By their very nature, job descriptions are fairly short and succinct. Without having pages to list every single job duty, company background, and so on, hiring managers will write what\u2019s most important at the top of the job description. It\u2019s there that they\u2019ll give you\u2014in either a sentence or two\u2014an overarching idea of what they want from their potential employee. As a job seeker, it\u2019s important for you to repeat that information (in your own words, of course) in your cover letter. Not only does it show that you read through the job description, but that you can do the work as well.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Respect the responsibilities.&lt;\/b&gt;\u00a0A typical job description might have upwards of ten or more job duties listed. Generally, the top five are the most critical ones and those that can make or break your job application. Make sure you actually can perform these duties, particularly if some of them are listed as \u201crequirements\u201d or \u201cqualifications.\u201d If you don\u2019t, your job application will be rejected by the Applicant Tracking System (ATS) or the actual person who is reading your resume.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Learn the lingo.&lt;\/b&gt;\u00a0Team player. Strong organizational skills. Leadership qualities. There are some terms that go hand in hand with a job description. But what do they really mean\u2014and do you really need to possess these skills and traits? A team player means that you\u2019ll be working with others, and you\u2019ll need to do so without any drama or complaining. Strong organizational skills is code for having a very busy workload and having to be able to manage it all well without dropping the ball\u2014or making your prospective boss look bad. If you\u2019re expected to have leadership qualities, you\u2019ll need to command the respect of your colleagues and lead and inspire them, which will require you to think outside of the box at times and be adaptable.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Share the love.&lt;\/b&gt;\u00a0In an effort to avoid being inundated with job applications, some companies will refrain from posting the company\u2019s name in the job description. If the company\u2019s name is listed, though, you should make a concerted effort to offer up some praise about the organization in your cover letter. If you\u2019re not very familiar with the company, do some research first, and then include a couple of sentences in your job application that depict how much you want to work for that specific organization. For example, you might write something like, \u201cI admire your organization\u2019s policy on workplace flexibility.\u201d After all, a boss is more apt to hire someone who specifically wants to work for his company as opposed to someone simply looking for any old job.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Find out the compensation.&lt;\/b&gt;\u00a0It\u2019s the question of any job seeker: how much does this job pay? Unfortunately, very few job postings will name a dollar amount. That doesn\u2019t mean you can\u2019t find out how much the company is willing to cough up for the position, though. By using sites such as salary.com, you can find out comparable salaries for the job you\u2019re after, and you can use this info to determine if it\u2019s worth applying for the position or not.\r\n\r\nWhen you\u2019re deep in the throes of your job search, it\u2019s easy to quickly scan a job description so that you can submit your application ASAP. But taking the time to thoroughly read through the posting can help you submit quality job applications that will get you hired for a position that you truly want\u2014and deserve.\r\n\r\n&nbsp;\r\n\r\n&lt;hr \/&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/04\/jennifer-parris.jpeg\"&gt;&lt;img class=\"alignleft size-full wp-image-13229\" src=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/04\/jennifer-parris.jpeg\" alt=\"Jennifer Parris, FlexJobs\" width=\"256\" height=\"256\" \/&gt;&lt;\/a&gt;&lt;b&gt;About the Author&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;i&gt;Jennifer Parris is a Career Writer for FlexJobs, an award-winning service that helps job-seekers find professional opportunities that offer work flexibility, such as telecommuting, freelance, part-time, or alternative schedules. To learn more about Jennifer, visit FlexJobs.com or tweet @flexjobs.&lt;\/i&gt;","post_title":"How to Read Between the Lines of a Job Description","post_excerpt":"","post_status":"publish","comment_status":"open","ping_status":"open","post_password":"","post_name":"how-to-read-between-the-lines-of-a-job-description","to_ping":"","pinged":"","post_modified":"2015-07-14 05:51:52","post_modified_gmt":"2015-07-14 12:51:52","post_content_filtered":"","post_parent":0,"guid":"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/?p=13227","menu_order":0,"post_type":"post","post_mime_type":"","comment_count":"0","filter":"raw"},{"ID":13303,"post_author":"4","post_date":"2015-07-09 02:00:03","post_date_gmt":"2015-07-09 09:00:03","post_content":"[media]&lt;img src=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/07\/7uy5tgef.jpg\" alt=\"Seasonal words to inspire writing.\" width=\"670\" height=\"350\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-15355\" \/&gt;[\/media]\r\n\r\n\"Summer afternoon, summer afternoon; to me those have always been the two most beautiful words in the English language,\" Henry James once wrote.\r\n\r\nWith the start of spring and the promise of summer, now is a good time to think about seasonal words. Writers, by nature, are collectors of words and catchy turns of phrase, but are there some that should be retired when they fall out of season? Look to literature for inspiration.\r\n\r\n&lt;strong&gt;Words for Spring&lt;\/strong&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;a href=\"https:\/\/www.flickr.com\/photos\/russellstreet\/7526097344\/sizes\/l\"&gt;&lt;img class=\" size-full wp-image-13305 aligncenter\" src=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/04\/Untitled8.png\" alt=\"seasons, trees, Grammarly\" width=\"600\" height=\"400\" \/&gt;&lt;\/a&gt;\r\n\r\nSpring is associated with birth and youth, and the emergence of color after drab winter days. &lt;i&gt;Vernal, verdant, fertile, burgeoning,&lt;\/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;callow&lt;\/i&gt; are favorite spring words, as are &lt;i&gt;blossoming, sprouting,&lt;\/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;bursting forth.&lt;\/i&gt; A line from Rainer Maria Rilke says it best: \"Spring has returned. The Earth is like a child that knows poems.\"\r\n\r\nSpring is also the perfect time to express &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.quickanddirtytips.com\/education\/grammar\/a-national-grammar-day-tale-of-love\"&gt;words of love&lt;\/a&gt;. Pablo Neruda, master of love poems, invokes spring themes: \"I want to do to you what spring does with the cherry trees.\" You can't help thinking of romance with spring-like phrases such as &lt;i&gt;breathe in&lt;\/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;come alive.&lt;\/i&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;strong&gt;Words for Summer&lt;\/strong&gt;\r\n\r\n\"In summer, the song sings itself,\" wrote William Carlos Williams. Summer is the season of daydreams, beach walks, and carefree afternoons soaking up the sun. &lt;i&gt;Languid, languorous,&lt;\/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;leisurely&lt;\/i&gt; are &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/2014\/shall-i-compare-thee-to-a-summers-day\/\"&gt;favorite summer words&lt;\/a&gt;, as are &lt;i&gt;jaunty, jovial,&lt;\/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;happy-go-lucky.&lt;\/i&gt;\r\n\r\nSummer is also the season of heat and passion. Think &lt;i&gt;sizzling, sweltering, searing,&lt;\/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;scorched.&lt;\/i&gt; In &lt;i&gt;Mad in Pursuit&lt;\/i&gt;, Violette Leduc describes summer well:\u00a0\"I walk without flinching through the burning cathedral of summer.\"\r\n\r\nOf course, no &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.quickanddirtytips.com\/education\/grammar\/12-common-words-that-will-boost-your-scrabble-score\"&gt;summer vocabulary&lt;\/a&gt; is complete without recreational words like &lt;i&gt;picnic, cookout, camp,&lt;\/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;vacation.&lt;\/i&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;strong&gt;Words for Autumn&lt;\/strong&gt;\r\n\r\nAutumn is the only season that has two names. The word &lt;i&gt;fall&lt;\/i&gt;\u00a0for the third season appeared in the 16th century; prior to that time, only summer and winter were defined seasons with names. &lt;i&gt;Spring&lt;\/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;fall&lt;\/i&gt; were shortened from \"spring of the leaf\" and \"fall of the leaf\" to define the in-between seasons.\r\n\r\nFall is the season of harvest, of crisp weather, and (of course) pumpkin spice latte. William Blake's &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.quickanddirtytips.com\/education\/grammar\/alphabet-of-errors-poem\"&gt;famous poem&lt;\/a&gt; \"To Autumn\" begins, \"Oh Autumn, laden with fruit and stained with the blood of the grape, pass not, but sit beneath my shady roof.\" Autumn is crackling, golden, and vibrant \u2013 a cornucopia of color.\r\n\r\n&lt;i&gt;Back to school sale,\u00a0Indian summer,&lt;\/i&gt;\u00a0and &lt;i&gt;pumpkin patch&lt;\/i&gt;\u00a0are uniquely autumn phrases that rarely get used once fall has passed.\r\n\r\n&lt;strong&gt;Words for Winter&lt;\/strong&gt;\r\n\r\nWhen winter comes, it brings words such as &lt;i&gt;snowflake, shiver, frostbite,&lt;\/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;flurry.&lt;\/i&gt; John Updike wrote of winter: \"The day is short, the sun a spark hung thin between the dark and dark.\" &lt;i&gt;Earmuffs, parka, mittens, boots&lt;\/i&gt;\u00a0\u2013 winter has its own wardrobe of words. It has its own menu, too: &lt;i&gt;hot cocoa, hearty stew, fruitcake, Christmas cookies,&lt;\/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;milk.&lt;\/i&gt;\r\n\r\nSome &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/2014\/how-to-keep-your-kids-writing-during-holiday-break\/\"&gt;winter words&lt;\/a&gt; melt away with spring: &lt;i&gt;icicle, hibernate, toboggan, snowball fight, wind chill factor,&lt;\/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;arctic blast.&lt;\/i&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;strong&gt;Words for Holidays&lt;\/strong&gt;\r\n\r\nEach holiday has a unique lexicon of seasonal words. New Year's Eve brings &lt;i&gt;resolutions&lt;\/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;Auld Lang Syne.&lt;\/i&gt;\u00a0April heralds &lt;i&gt;Easter bunnies&lt;\/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;Easter bonnets, egg rolls&lt;\/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;egg hunts,&lt;\/i&gt; and the iconic &lt;i&gt;marshmallow Peep.&lt;\/i&gt; In July, we get &lt;i&gt;fireworks, parades,&lt;\/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;patriotism&lt;\/i&gt; wrapped in the American flag. Christmas is the mother lode: &lt;i&gt;Santa, mistletoe, Black Friday, eggnog, nutcracker, Scrooge, tinsel, wassail, carol,&lt;\/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;Yule.&lt;\/i&gt;\r\n\r\nMost words are evergreen and show up all year round, but some words evoke seasonal memories and feel out of place when they're used out of turn. &lt;i&gt;Pumpkin pie&lt;\/i&gt; and &lt;i&gt;picnic,&lt;\/i&gt; for example, elicits a seasonal disconnect.\r\n\r\nWhat are some of your favorite words to conjure up a warm spring day or a cold winter night?","post_title":"\"Seasonal\" Words: Do They Exist?","post_excerpt":"","post_status":"publish","comment_status":"open","ping_status":"open","post_password":"","post_name":"seasonal-words-do-they-exist","to_ping":"","pinged":"","post_modified":"2015-07-09 08:29:29","post_modified_gmt":"2015-07-09 15:29:29","post_content_filtered":"","post_parent":0,"guid":"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/?p=13303","menu_order":0,"post_type":"post","post_mime_type":"","comment_count":"0","filter":"raw"},{"ID":13297,"post_author":"4","post_date":"2015-07-07 02:00:18","post_date_gmt":"2015-07-07 09:00:18","post_content":"[media]&lt;img src=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/07\/iphone-evening.jpg\" alt=\"Here&#039;s how to be nicer on the phone\" width=\"670\" height=\"350\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-15325\" \/&gt;[\/media]\r\n\r\nCell phones hit the free market 30 years ago, but Americans still haven't internalized a complete set of social rules for cell phone usage. If you're not sure what's acceptable in the world of cell phone etiquette, check out these five tips in honor of Cell Phone Courtesy Month in July.\r\n\r\n&lt;strong&gt;Keep Private Conversations Private&lt;\/strong&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;a rel=\"no follow\" href=\"https:\/\/www.flickr.com\/photos\/edenpictures\/3385862821\/sizes\/m\/\"&gt;&lt;img class=\" size-full wp-image-13299 aligncenter\" src=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/04\/Untitled7.png\" alt=\"Image via Flickr by edenpictures\" width=\"500\" height=\"400\" \/&gt;&lt;\/a&gt;\r\n\r\nWhen you're engrossed in a phone conversation, it's easy to fool yourself into believing that no one can hear you except the person on the other end of the line.\r\n\r\nIn truth, anyone within 10\u00a0feet can hear your half of the conversation, and whether they mean to or not, they're bound to follow along. It doesn't matter if you're wandering the aisles of the grocery store or huddled inside your work cubicle; others'\u00a0ears perk up at the hint of a private exchange. If you don\u2019t want the other patrons of Starbucks to hear about your recent dermatological exam, don\u2019t call your mom with the details as you\u2019re waiting for your morning latte.\r\n\r\n&lt;strong&gt;Avoid Toilet Talk&lt;\/strong&gt;\r\n\r\nData suggests that up to 87 percent of all people have texted or chatted on the phone &lt;a rel=\"no follow\" href=\"http:\/\/www.nydailynews.com\/life-style\/health\/cell-phone-bathroom-75-americans-admit-calling-texting-toilet-article-1.1015634\"&gt;while sitting on the toilet&lt;\/a&gt;. While it may be acceptable to do this in the privacy of home, it's just plain rude to talk on the phone in a public bathroom. People visiting the lavatory expect privacy. Wielding your cell phone while others answer nature's call is like filming an impromptu movie in a public locker room. You wouldn't bring a live mic into a bathroom stall. Don't bring your cell phone, either.\r\n\r\n&lt;strong&gt;Exercise Caution With Text-Speak&lt;\/strong&gt;\r\n\r\nTexting is still a &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/2015\/brb-im-learning-these-grammar-rules-for-texting\/\"&gt;seedling technology&lt;\/a&gt;, and society hasn't adopted a definitive consensus as to what's acceptable yet. However, if you suspect a person might feel annoyed or inconvenienced by your texting language, you might want to mind your p's and q's.\r\n\r\nIf you need to text a boss, coworker, or professional acquaintance, don't use the same language and abbreviations you would use when texting a friend. Though \"text speak\" (K, LOL, etc.) is quick and easy, you sacrifice professionalism and credibility when you use it for work purposes.\r\n\r\nThough it is occasionally acceptable to throw an \"OMW\" or \"SMH\" into your daily texts, you should practice using correct punctuation, spelling, and grammar when texting. After all, you don't want to confuse Grandma with your trendy text speak or offend anyone when you say \"LMFAO.\"\r\n\r\n&lt;strong&gt;Don't Dial and Drive&lt;\/strong&gt;\r\n\r\nIn certain areas of the country, driving with a cell phone in hand is &lt;a rel=\"no follow\" href=\"http:\/\/www.ghsa.org\/html\/stateinfo\/laws\/cellphone_laws.html\"&gt;illegal&lt;\/a&gt;.\u00a0Even if you live in a state where the cops can't arrest you for it, dialing and driving is considered rude by plenty of people.\r\n\r\nWhy do some people frown upon dialing and driving? Perhaps it's due to the fact that distracted driving claims the lives of at least &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.cdc.gov\/motorvehiclesafety\/distracted_driving\/\"&gt;nine people per day&lt;\/a&gt; in the U.S., according to the Centers for Disease Control.\u00a0To these folks, talking on the phone while driving is akin to saying, \"My phone call is more important than your life.\"\r\n\r\nIndeed, that's rather rude.\r\n\r\n&lt;strong&gt;Don't Text and Drive&lt;\/strong&gt;\r\n\r\nWhile driving and dialing might fall into a gray area of acceptability, driving and texting is never okay. It doesn't matter how careful and coordinated you are; texting removes your hands from the wheel, your eyes from the road, and your mind from what you're doing.\r\n\r\nIn fact, \"&lt;a rel=\"no follow\" href=\"http:\/\/www.textinganddrivingsafety.com\/texting-and-driving-stats\/\"&gt;driving while intexticated&lt;\/a&gt;\" has grown into a national epidemic. Some claim that it's a cinch for them to text and drive. However, these people may not realize that texting causes over 1\u00a0million crashes per year \u2013 and the trend isn't improving.\r\n\r\nIn the majority of social situations, norms guide behavior. However, with cell phone usage, norms are still evolving. Are you guilty of breaking any of these rules of cell phone etiquette?","post_title":"5 Cell Phone Etiquette Tips","post_excerpt":"","post_status":"publish","comment_status":"open","ping_status":"open","post_password":"","post_name":"5-cell-phone-etiquette-tips","to_ping":"","pinged":"","post_modified":"2015-07-07 08:29:37","post_modified_gmt":"2015-07-07 15:29:37","post_content_filtered":"","post_parent":0,"guid":"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/?p=13297","menu_order":0,"post_type":"post","post_mime_type":"","comment_count":"0","filter":"raw"},{"ID":13291,"post_author":"4","post_date":"2015-07-02 02:00:57","post_date_gmt":"2015-07-02 09:00:57","post_content":"[media]&lt;img src=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/07\/45tfrds5rtf.jpg\" alt=\"7 Words\/Phrases Used Differently as Years Go By\" width=\"670\" height=\"350\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-15245\" \/&gt;[\/media]\r\n\r\nRead a piece of literature from a couple hundred years ago \u2014 or even just a few decades ago \u2014 and you might feel like you're reading a different dialect of English. &lt;a rel=\"no follow\" href=\"http:\/\/ed.ted.com\/lessons\/how-languages-evolve-alex-gendler\"&gt;Languages evolve&lt;\/a&gt;, usually &lt;a rel=\"no follow\" href=\"http:\/\/www.rosettastone.com\/blog\/language-myths-and-complicated-languages\/\"&gt;becoming simpler&lt;\/a&gt; over time. Acceptable grammar practices change, writing styles shift, and words and phrases take on meanings that may be a significant departure from their original definition.\r\n\r\nOne common example of a word with a new meaning is \"gay.\" You might often hear traditionalists point out that the word previously meant happy, and it had nothing to do with a person's sexual orientation. Of course, that is one example among hundreds; here are a few more words that have different meanings today than they did in yesteryear.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Awful&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\n\"Awesome\" and \"awful\" &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/2014\/these-words-may-sound-similar-but-they-have-very-different-meanings\/\"&gt;sound similar&lt;\/a&gt;, but they have opposite meanings \u2014 today. However, if you take a trip in the way-back machine, you'll find that \"awful\" really wasn't so bad. In fact, it used to describe something that inspired awe, something jaw-dropping in a good way. Next time you want to give a creative compliment, use awful in its original sense. Just make sure you explain what you really mean.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Broadcast&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;a rel=\"no follow\" href=\"https:\/\/www.flickr.com\/photos\/bluecorvette\/8265586126\/sizes\/m\/\"&gt;&lt;img class=\"alignleft size-full wp-image-13293\" src=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/04\/Untitled6.png\" alt=\"farm, broadcast, Grammarly\" width=\"500\" height=\"375\" \/&gt;&lt;\/a&gt;\r\n\r\nTelevision and radio stations transmit their content to a wide audience, and this is how we most often define \"broadcasting.\" However, the word has its roots in agriculture. Instead of meticulously planting each seed, a worker would scatter seed by tossing it in handfuls on primed soil. Even today, there are broadcasting machines that distribute grass seed and fertilizer.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Fantastic&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\nHe can stretch for miles, and he leads a team of superheroes. He is Mr. Fantastic, and he lives up to his name in every sense of the word \u2014\u00a0according to both the archaic and modern meanings of it. Today, \u201cfantastic\u201d describes something that is outstandingly good, something above and beyond the everyday. However, it used to have a meaning more directly related to its root word, \"fantasy.\" Yep, fantastic once referred only to things that don't exist.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Backlog&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\nToday, \"backlog\" refers to mountains of work that probably require an all-nighter or two to finish. Are you wondering about the word's original meaning? In colonial times, a &lt;a rel=\"no follow\"  href=\"http:\/\/www.huffingtonpost.com\/2014\/02\/26\/words-that-have-changed-meaning_n_4847343.html\"&gt;backlog&lt;\/a&gt; was the biggest log in the fire. Go ahead, throw a backlog in the fireplace, grab some coffee, and get started on that backlog of paperwork.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Villain&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\nIf you like to write fiction, you probably pour hours into crafting the perfect villain. You come up with a potent back story, outstanding characteristics, and a sinister list of to-do's. Well, if you lived in the 13&lt;sup&gt;th&lt;\/sup&gt; or 14&lt;sup&gt;th&lt;\/sup&gt; century, you wouldn't put so much effort into the villains of your novel unless you were writing a gripping tale of life on a farm. That's right; a villain was nothing more than a farmhand.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Passenger&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\nIf you're a passenger in a car or bus, you might look out the window and see pedestrians, but those folks on the sidewalk are passengers, too, according to the &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.buzzfeed.com\/awesomer\/words-that-used-to-mean-something-totally-different\"&gt;word's old meaning&lt;\/a&gt;. Passengers were originally people who traveled by foot.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Pedant&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\nBack in the 19&lt;sup&gt;th&lt;\/sup&gt; century, published works used this word about &lt;a rel=\"no follow\"  href=\"https:\/\/books.google.com\/ngrams\/graph?content=pedant&amp;year_start=1800&amp;year_end=2000&amp;corpus=15&amp;smoothing=3&amp;share=&amp;direct_url=t1%3B%2Cpedant%3B%2Cc0\"&gt;six times as frequently&lt;\/a&gt; as they do today, and that isn't the only way that \"pedant\" has changed over the years. It used to describe a knowledgeable person, a schoolmaster. Today it refers to someone who is a little too concerned about details.\r\n\r\nLanguage, like culture, must adapt to new attitudes and new ways of thinking. That is why so many words do not mean what they used to. Can you think of any other interesting examples of words or phrases that have left behind their original meanings?","post_title":"7 Words\/Phrases That Don\u2019t Mean What You Think They Mean","post_excerpt":"","post_status":"publish","comment_status":"open","ping_status":"open","post_password":"","post_name":"7-wordsphrases-that-dont-mean-what-you-think-they-mean","to_ping":"","pinged":"","post_modified":"2015-07-02 09:24:53","post_modified_gmt":"2015-07-02 16:24:53","post_content_filtered":"","post_parent":0,"guid":"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/?p=13291","menu_order":0,"post_type":"post","post_mime_type":"","comment_count":"0","filter":"raw"},{"ID":13247,"post_author":"4","post_date":"2015-06-18 02:00:34","post_date_gmt":"2015-06-18 09:00:34","post_content":"[media]&lt;img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-14931\" src=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/06\/23esagfd.jpg\" alt=\"Grammarly Quotations\" width=\"670\" height=\"350\" \/&gt;[\/media]\r\nWhat does it mean to be a father? Dads approach fatherhood in a variety of ways, from overbearing to \u201cwrapped around your little finger,\u201d and everything in between. There\u2019s no formula for the perfect father, but there are some commonalities among father figures in literature that make the concept of fatherhood a powerful one.\r\n\r\nIn honor of &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/2014\/what-to-write-for-fathers-day\/\"&gt;Father's Day&lt;\/a&gt;, here are six father figures in literature. Which reminds you of your own father?\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;King Lear, The \u201cPrideful\u201d Father&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\nThe life of the title character in Shakespeare's &lt;i&gt;King Lear&lt;\/i&gt; is shaped by his three daughters. When it comes time for him to step down from the throne in his old age, King Lear makes a drastic mistake. Instead of dividing his empire evenly among his three daughters, a final deceit causes him to disown Cordelia. Unfortunately, King Lear doesn't realize that Cordelia loved him most until it's too late. Despite this tragic choice, King Lear's powerful love for his daughters defines his life.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Mr. Bennet, The \u201cProtective\u201d Father&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.huffingtonpost.com\/allison-pataki\/top-ten-father-figures-in_b_5488200.html\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;Mr. Bennet&lt;\/a&gt; may not be the richest character in Jane Austen's &lt;i&gt;Pride and Prejudice&lt;\/i&gt;, but what makes him a memorable father is the constant care and empathy that he shows for his daughters. Given the Bennet family\u2019s financial situation, he feels pressure to marry his daughters off, but instead of focusing on money he keeps his children's best interests in mind. Throughout the novel, it's clear how much Mr. Bennet admires his daughter Lizzy, in particular, in the way he uses both his wisdom and humor to guide her through difficult life decisions.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Bob Cratchit, The \u201cOptimistic\u201d Father&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\nThe majority of Charles Dickens' &lt;em&gt;A Christmas Carol&lt;\/em&gt; focuses on the eternally grumpy Ebeneezer Scrooge and the unfortunate Tiny Tim. The unsung hero here, however, is Tiny Tim's father, &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.bridgemanimages.com\/en-US\/explore\/news\/features\/2013\/June\/top-10-father-figures-from-literature\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;Bob Cratchit&lt;\/a&gt;. As Scrooge's employee, Cratchit can't see much light at the end of the tunnel, and he is perpetually kept cold and underpaid. Instead of giving up, Cratchit makes the best of the situation and dutifully reports to work in order to take care of his beloved son. After a spiritual intervention, Scrooge makes a turn for the better and Cratchit's persistence and steadfastness pays off.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Atticus Finch, The \u201cRole Model\u201d Father&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;a href=\"https:\/\/www.flickr.com\/photos\/x-ray_delta_one\/5899419289\/sizes\/m\/\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;&lt;img class=\"alignleft size-medium wp-image-13249\" src=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/04\/Untitled2-319x410.png\" alt=\"Image via Flickr by x-ray delta one\" width=\"319\" height=\"410\" \/&gt;&lt;\/a&gt;\r\n\r\nDespite tough times, &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/blog.chegg.com\/2013\/06\/14\/10-of-the-best-fictional-fathers\/\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;Atticus Finch&lt;\/a&gt; serves as a father figure to admire in Harper Lee's &lt;i&gt;To Kill a Mockingbird&lt;\/i&gt;. A widower and lawyer in the Jim Crow South, Finch does his best to be his children's moral compass. Perhaps the best example of this is the way Finch encourages his children to be who they want to be instead of what their troubled society says is right. Instead of forcing his daughter to be a girly girl, Finch encourages Scout to develop her tomboy personality. He has a challenging road in front of him, but he remains a pillar of strength throughout the novel.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Calvin's Dad, The \u201cPatient\u201d Father&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\nFor years, fans enjoyed Bill Watterson's funny and sweet comic strip, &lt;i&gt;Calvin and Hobbes&lt;\/i&gt;. A calm and collected counterpoint to the mischievous Calvin, his dad proves time and time again that patience is a virtue. Throughout many story lines, &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/gliterature.com\/2011\/06\/19\/top-5-fictional-fathers\/\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;Calvin's dad&lt;\/a&gt; answers his son's often-obnoxious questions and deals with his many well-intentioned mishaps. Best of all, he loves Calvin through all of his trying moments and troublesome times.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;The Man, The \u201cSacrificing\u201d Father&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;i&gt;The Road&lt;\/i&gt; by Cormac McCarthy is a post-apocalyptic novel that remains grim from cover to cover, but one of the shining lights throughout is &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.shortlist.com\/entertainment\/books\/30-most-memorable-literary-fathers\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;The Man&lt;\/a&gt;. This father figure doesn't have a lot to offer his son, due to their extraordinary circumstances. Instead, he does everything he can to keep his son alive and motivated along their incredibly difficult journey through what seems like the end of the world.\r\n\r\nThese father figures demonstrate a full range of parenting styles throughout &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.quickanddirtytips.com\/education\/grammar\/how-literature-changes-your-brain-for-the-better\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;centuries of literature&lt;\/a&gt;. What unifies them is their dedication to their children and their insistence on placing their kids and their families first and foremost. Which father figure do you find most inspiring?\r\n\r\n&nbsp;","post_title":"Who Is Your Literary \u201cFather Figure?\u201d","post_excerpt":"","post_status":"publish","comment_status":"open","ping_status":"open","post_password":"","post_name":"who-is-your-literary-father-figure","to_ping":"","pinged":"","post_modified":"2015-06-23 13:55:05","post_modified_gmt":"2015-06-23 20:55:05","post_content_filtered":"","post_parent":0,"guid":"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/?p=13247","menu_order":0,"post_type":"post","post_mime_type":"","comment_count":"0","filter":"raw"},{"ID":13239,"post_author":"4","post_date":"2015-06-16 02:00:29","post_date_gmt":"2015-06-16 09:00:29","post_content":"[media]&lt;img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-14871\" src=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/06\/car-games.jpg\" alt=\"Car Games\" width=\"670\" height=\"350\" \/&gt;[\/media]\r\n\r\nStiff legs. Sore behind. \"Are we there yet, Mom?\"\r\n\r\nIt doesn't matter whether you're going to Aspen, New Orleans, or Disney World. Long car rides bore the best of us. One of the fastest ways to bust boredom is to &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.livescience.com\/23493-why-we-get-bored.html\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;keep your mind active&lt;\/a&gt;. Pack these nifty word-related car games in your overnight bag the next time you hit the road.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Character Sketches&lt;\/b&gt;\r\nChoose another car and take a good look at its passengers. Each person makes up a backstory about the passengers in the other vehicle and shares it with the others.\r\n\r\nIf you're stumped, start by answering these questions about the folks in the other car:\r\n&lt;p style=\"padding-left: 60px;\"&gt;1. Who are they?\r\n2. Where are they going?\r\n3. What are their hopes and fears?\r\n4. What are their flaws and strengths?&lt;\/p&gt;\r\nFiction writers use &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/2014\/embrace-your-geekness-with-the-character-sketch\/\"&gt;character sketches&lt;\/a&gt; to spur their creativity. These thumbnails often morph into the fascinating characters we meet it books. You can do it, too \u2013 on wheels.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;License Plate Decoding Game&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;a href=\"https:\/\/www.flickr.com\/photos\/gammaman\/9114536420\/sizes\/m\/\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;&lt;img class=\"alignleft size-full wp-image-13241\" src=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/04\/Untitled1.png\" alt=\"License Plate, Grammarly, car games, road trip\" width=\"500\" height=\"375\" \/&gt;&lt;\/a&gt;\r\n\r\nWhat if every license plate harbored a secret meaning within its letters and numbers? That's the premise behind the License Plate Decoding Game. The game works especially well when you're caught in traffic because you have plenty of time to peruse and \"decode\" the license plates around you.\r\n\r\nFor example:\r\n&lt;p style=\"padding-left: 90px;\"&gt;\u2022 \"PTA 247\" becomes \"Peanut butter tastes awesome to 47-year-olds.\"\r\n\u2022 \"YHB 711\" becomes \"Your hair looks bad seven days a week, eleven hours a day.\"&lt;\/p&gt;\r\n&lt;b&gt;License Plate School&lt;\/b&gt;\r\nIf you're traveling with little ones, consider using license plates to reinforce geography and phonics lessons learned at school. &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.edmunds.com\/car-reviews\/top-10\/top-10-road-trip-games.html\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;Edmunds.com&lt;\/a&gt; suggests that children \"collect\" plates from the different states or try to find all the letters of the alphabet - first forwards, then backwards.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Related Words Game&lt;\/b&gt;\r\nThe Related Words Game requires each player to brainstorm a list of words that relate to a specific starting word. The subsequent list must bring the topic back full circle. Whoever creates the shortest list wins.\r\n\r\nFor example, Player One might create a list like this:\r\n&lt;p style=\"padding-left: 90px;\"&gt;\u2022 noodles\r\n\u2022 delicious food\r\n\u2022 cake\r\n\u2022 birthday cake\r\n\u2022 presents\r\n\u2022 wrapping paper\r\n\u2022 ribbons\r\n\u2022 strings\r\n\u2022 noodles&lt;\/p&gt;\r\nPlayer Two might create a list like this:\r\n&lt;p style=\"padding-left: 90px;\"&gt;\u2022 noodles\r\n\u2022 yellow\r\n\u2022 egg yolks\r\n\u2022 chicken\r\n\u2022 chicken noodle soup\r\n\u2022 noodles&lt;\/p&gt;\r\nBecause Player Two created the shorter list, he\/she wins. You can play as many rounds of the Related Words Game as you like, but if you wish to limit the game, choose a random word like PIG. Each time someone loses a round, they take one letter of the word. For example, Player One earned a \"P\" for this round. Whoever spells the word \"PIG\" first loses the game.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Round Robin Story Game&lt;\/b&gt;\r\nTeachers have used &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.edutopia.org\/blog\/alternatives-to-round-robin-reading-todd-finley\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;round robin reading strategies&lt;\/a&gt; in the classroom for decades. In this game, car riders use the round-robin style to create a groupthink story. Each rider contributes one word at a time. The entire story lasts four or five sentences. If possible, choose a scribe to write or record the words as they are generated.\r\n\r\nIf a player thinks a sentence sounds complete, any passenger can &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/handbook\/punctuation\/\"&gt;insert punctuation&lt;\/a&gt; by shouting \"Period!\" or \"Exclamation point!\"\r\n\r\nHere's an example of an opening sentence created by a four-person car load:\r\n&lt;p style=\"padding-left: 90px;\"&gt;Person 1: Once\r\nPerson 2: upon\r\nPerson 3: a\r\nPerson 4: time\r\nPerson 1: I\r\nPerson 2: ate\r\nPerson 3: twenty-six\r\nPerson 4: frogs\r\nPerson 1: and\r\nPerson 2: turned\r\nPerson 3: into\r\nPerson: 4: a\r\nPerson 1: wombat.\r\n(PERIOD)&lt;\/p&gt;\r\nNo matter how silly the story gets, each word must make &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/mentalfloss.com\/article\/49238\/7-sentences-sound-crazy-are-still-grammatical\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;grammatical sense&lt;\/a&gt; in the context of the story.\r\n\r\nVacations are essential for happiness and well-being, but getting to your vacation spot can be tedious. How will you break up the monotony during your next long car ride?","post_title":"5 Word-Related Car Games for Your Next Road Trip","post_excerpt":"","post_status":"publish","comment_status":"open","ping_status":"open","post_password":"","post_name":"5-word-related-car-games-for-your-next-road-trip","to_ping":"","pinged":"","post_modified":"2015-06-16 06:17:25","post_modified_gmt":"2015-06-16 13:17:25","post_content_filtered":"","post_parent":0,"guid":"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/?p=13239","menu_order":0,"post_type":"post","post_mime_type":"","comment_count":"0","filter":"raw"},{"ID":14837,"post_author":"6","post_date":"2015-06-14 09:18:27","post_date_gmt":"2015-06-14 16:18:27","post_content":"[media]&lt;img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-14839\" src=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/06\/t5r4fdw6yt.jpg\" alt=\"EOD\" width=\"670\" height=\"350\" \/&gt;[\/media]\r\n\r\nWhether you\u2019re just gearing up for business school or you\u2019ve been in your industry for a long time, it\u2019s a good idea to be familiar with what certain business terms mean. Here are 10 words and abbreviations every businessperson needs to know.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;ROI: return on investment.&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n&lt;i&gt;When push comes to shove, we\u2019ll prioritize the project with the highest ROI.&lt;\/i&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;USP: unique selling position.&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n&lt;i&gt;The marketing team worked hard to develop the company\u2019s USP so that the sales team would have more to work with. &lt;\/i&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Forecast: to use data you\u2019ve gathered to predict future trends.&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n&lt;i&gt;Based on our sales numbers from last year, we can forecast and set our budgets for the third and fourth quarters.&lt;\/i&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Balance sheet: a summary of the company\u2019s accounts including assets, liabilities, and equity.&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n&lt;i&gt;Let\u2019s take a look at the balance sheet again before Thursday\u2019s investor meeting.&lt;\/i&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Brand: a company\u2019s logo, tagline, or other distinguishing identifier that sets them apart in the marketplace.&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n&lt;i&gt;In today\u2019s meeting, we\u2019ll decide on which colors to use for our brand.&lt;\/i&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Minutes: notes from a meeting, including what was said and what actions will be taken next.&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n&lt;i&gt;Please review the meeting minutes from last week before joining the conference call.&lt;\/i&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Stakeholder: any individual or group who has a stake (interest) in the company or project.&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n&lt;i&gt;I emailed the relevant stakeholders to get their feedback on our new marketing initiative.&lt;\/i&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;B2B and B2C: business-to-business and business-to-consumer.&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n&lt;i&gt;As a B2B company, we only spend a small portion of our budget on widespread advertising.&lt;\/i&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;EOD: end of day.&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n&lt;i&gt;I\u2019ll have that report in your inbox by EOD.&lt;\/i&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Performance or annual review: An evaluation and assessment of an employee\u2019s contributions to the company.&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n&lt;i&gt;During her annual review, she was offered a promotion and a bonus.&lt;\/i&gt;\r\n\r\nWhich words would you add to this list?","post_title":"10 words and abbreviations you need to know for business school","post_excerpt":"","post_status":"publish","comment_status":"open","ping_status":"open","post_password":"","post_name":"10-words-and-abbreviations-you-need-to-know-for-business-school","to_ping":"","pinged":"","post_modified":"2015-06-14 16:18:27","post_content_filtered":"","post_parent":0,"guid":"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/?p=14837","menu_order":0,"post_type":"post","post_mime_type":"","comment_count":"0","filter":"raw"},{"ID":14823,"post_author":"6","post_date":"2015-06-12 07:38:09","post_date_gmt":"2015-06-12 14:38:09","post_content":"[media]&lt;img src=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/06\/234t5gfc.jpg\" alt=\"What are you reading?\" width=\"670\" height=\"350\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-14827\" \/&gt;[\/media]\r\n\r\nEach year, the American Library Association honors outstanding books relating to the lesbian, gay, bisexual, and transgender experience with the Stonewall Book Awards. In celebration of Pride Month, here are a few selections from that list.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Bitter Eden&lt;\/i&gt; by Tatamkhulu Afrika&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n&lt;i&gt;Bitter Eden&lt;\/i&gt; tells the story of prisoners of war through their own eyes and delves into the nuances of the bonds they forge with each other.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;I'll Give You the Sun&lt;\/i&gt; by Jandy Nelson &lt;\/b&gt;\r\nTold from the perspective of twin siblings, &lt;i&gt;I\u2019ll Give You the Sun&lt;\/i&gt; is a story about growing up and growing apart but finding a way to come back together again.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Two Boys Kissing&lt;\/i&gt; by David Levithan&lt;\/b&gt;\r\nTwo boys set out to break the Guinness World Record for marathon kissing. What happens along the way touches and shapes the lives of many people around them.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;Aristotle and Dante Discover the Secrets of the Universe&lt;\/i&gt; by Benjamin Alire Saenz&lt;\/b&gt;\r\nA beautifully written coming-of-age story, &lt;i&gt;Aristotle and Dante&lt;\/i&gt; delves into the internal and external struggles of a teenager trying to find out who he is and determine his place in the world.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;&lt;i&gt;The Unreal Life of Sergey Nabokov&lt;\/i&gt; by Paul Russell &lt;\/b&gt;\r\nBased on the life of novelist Vladamir Nabokov\u2019s brother, this novel tells the story of Sergey and his incredible life in pre-World War II Europe, including his relationships with Gertrude Stein, Alice B. Toklas, and Picasso.\r\n\r\n&lt;hr \/&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;i&gt;June is Lesbian, Gay, Bisexual and Transgender (LGBT) Pride Month. Celebrate human rights, tolerance, and equality with us throughout the month! #PrideMonth&lt;\/i&gt;","post_title":"5 Award-winning books featuring LGBT characters","post_excerpt":"","post_status":"publish","comment_status":"open","ping_status":"open","post_password":"","post_name":"5-award-winning-books-featuring-lgbt-characters","to_ping":"","pinged":"","post_modified":"2015-06-12 07:38:09","post_modified_gmt":"2015-06-12 14:38:09","post_content_filtered":"","post_parent":0,"guid":"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/?p=14823","menu_order":0,"post_type":"post","post_mime_type":"","comment_count":"0","filter":"raw"},{"ID":12425,"post_author":"4","post_date":"2015-06-11 02:00:12","post_date_gmt":"2015-06-11 09:00:12","post_content":"[media]&lt;img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-14819\" src=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/06\/234redsa.jpg\" alt=\"5 LGBTQI Authors Who Have Made an Impact\" width=\"670\" height=\"350\" \/&gt;[\/media]\r\n\r\nIt's no secret that some of the finest pieces of literature ever written were authored by members of the LGBT community. From the poetry of Walt Whitman to the landmark plays of Tony Kushner, it's impossible to overstate the impact LGBT authors have had in American literature. In honor of Pride Month, here are five of the most important and influential LGBT writers of all time.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Oscar Wilde&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.biography.com\/people\/oscar-wilde-9531078\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;Oscar Wilde&lt;\/a&gt;, a prolific Irish author whose poems, essays, and plays remain relevant more than 100 years after his death, wrote just one novel, \"The Portrait of Dorian Gray.\" The novel provoked a public outcry over what was perceived as a stunning lack of morality. Wilde, perhaps Britain's leading proponent of the Aesthetic Movement, defended his &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/2014\/7-novels-to-read-for-a-better-vocabulary\/\"&gt;novel &lt;\/a&gt;in its preface,\u00a0stating, \"ethical sympathy in an artist is an unpardonable mannerism of style.\" Later, he wrote, \"Vice and virtue are to the artist materials for an art.\"\r\n\r\nWilde was arrested on charges of public indecency for his open homosexuality and served two years in prison. He died at 46, penniless and in exile in France.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Tennessee Williams&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\nBorn Thomas Lanier Williams in 1911, &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.biography.com\/people\/tennessee-williams-9532952\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;Tennessee Williams&lt;\/a&gt;\u00a0is considered one of America's best playwrights of the 20th century. His iconic \"Streetcar Named Desire\" earned Williams both a Pulitzer Prize and a Drama Critics Award. Other important successes include \"The Glass Menagerie,\" \"Cat on a Hot Tin Roof,\" and \"Orpheus Descending,\" which was made into a movie (\"The Fugitive Kind\") starring Marlon Brando.\r\n\r\nWilliams was openly gay, even suffering a hate attack in Key West in 1979. The author lapsed into a period of alcoholism and drug use and was found dead in 1983 at the age of 71.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Virginia Woolf&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\nWoolf's most famous work, \"&lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.theguardian.com\/books\/2014\/sep\/01\/100-best-novels-mrs-dalloway-virginia-woolf-robert-mccrum\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;Mrs. Dalloway&lt;\/a&gt;,\" earned the bisexual author a prominent role in contemporary American literature; in 2005, &lt;em&gt;Time&lt;\/em&gt; magazine placed it in the top 100 English-language novels of the past century. Woolf suffered sexual abuse early in her life at the hands of half-brothers; her battle with mental illness and depression throughout her life influenced her work. \"Mrs. Dalloway,\" written in mesmerizing prose, raises emerging social issues, such as feminism and homosexuality.\r\n\r\nWoolf ultimately succumbed to her depression and committed suicide at the age of 59 by filling her pockets with stones and walking into the River Ouse.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Alice Walker&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\nA committed social activist, teacher, and lecturer, &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/lesbianlife.about.com\/od\/artistswriterset1\/p\/Pulitzer-Prize-Winning-Author-Alice-Walker.htm\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;Alice Walker's prolific writing career&lt;\/a&gt; spans more than four decades. Her works encompass novels, short stories, children's books, &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.quickanddirtytips.com\/education\/grammar\/a-funny-story-about-epic-poetry\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;poems&lt;\/a&gt;, and essays; she is most famous for the groundbreaking and critically acclaimed \"The Color Purple,\" which earned Walker a Pulitzer Prize and a National Book Award. Many of Walker's works promote themes of the black feminist movement and explore issues related to race and gender identity.\r\n\r\nOther &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/2015\/words-of-wisdom-from-great-women-writers\/?sf\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;highly influential works&lt;\/a&gt; include \"The Temple of My Familiar\" and \"Possessing the Secret of Joy.\"\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Chuck Palahniuk&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\nThis author's pointed, minimalistic &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.quickanddirtytips.com\/education\/grammar\/style-and-register\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;writing style&lt;\/a&gt; has earned both praise and criticism and his works often explore controversial themes such as morality, sexuality, and religion. His most famous work is \"Fight Club,\" a novel that was made into a movie starring Brad Pitt; his widely acclaimed novel \"Choke\" was his first book to make the &lt;em&gt;New York Times&lt;\/em&gt; best seller list.\r\n\r\n&lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.brainyquote.com\/quotes\/authors\/c\/chuck_palahniuk.html\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;Palahniuk's writing&lt;\/a&gt; is influenced by giants such as Albert Camus, Michel Foucault, Thom Spanbauer, and Bret Easton Ellis. He is also a freelance journalist and &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.quickanddirtytips.com\/productivity\/project-management\/set-intermediate-deadlines-to-stay-on-track\" rel=\"no follow\"&gt;essayist&lt;\/a&gt;.\r\n\r\nWhile not all LGBT authors write\u00a0about sexuality and gender, the classic works mentioned above reflect the uniquely valuable LGBT perspective. &lt;i&gt;Do you have a favorite LGBT author or work that deals with LGBT issues?&lt;\/i&gt;\r\n\r\n&nbsp;\r\n\r\n&lt;hr \/&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;i&gt;June is Lesbian, Gay, Bisexual and Transgender (LGBT) Pride Month. Celebrate human rights, tolerance, and equality with us throughout the month! #PrideMonth &lt;\/i&gt;","post_title":"5 LGBT Authors Who Have Made an Impact","post_excerpt":"","post_status":"publish","comment_status":"open","ping_status":"open","post_password":"","post_name":"5-lgbt-authors-who-have-made-an-impact","to_ping":"","pinged":"","post_modified":"2015-06-11 08:50:02","post_modified_gmt":"2015-06-11 15:50:02","post_content_filtered":"","post_parent":0,"guid":"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/?p=12425","menu_order":0,"post_type":"post","post_mime_type":"","comment_count":"0","filter":"raw"},{"ID":12415,"post_author":"4","post_date":"2015-06-09 02:00:35","post_date_gmt":"2015-06-09 09:00:35","post_content":"[media]&lt;img src=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/06\/adidas.jpg\" alt=\"Brand Knock-Offs Image\" width=\"600\" height=\"314\" class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-14767\" \/&gt;[\/media]\r\n\r\nOne of the best things about language is its malleability. You can &lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/2015\/spelling-counts-make-sure-you-use-these-words-correctly\/?sf\"&gt;switch around a few letters&lt;\/a&gt;, relocate a comma, or replace a pronoun, and you've suddenly changed the meaning of a sentence. The same principle applies to product logos. A small change can make a big \u2014 and hilarious \u2014 difference. Here is a short list of some side-splittingly funny product knock-offs from around the world.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Sunbucks Coffee&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\nRealistically, the name Sunbucks\u00a0makes more sense for a coffee shop than Starbucks, right? After all, more people drink coffee in the morning than they do at night. Sunbucks in China serves up coffee under a logo\u00a0like\u00a0Starbucks, but instead of the goddess Siren as their logo, they use a crazy-looking dog.\r\n\r\nAs if Sunbucks isn't enough, Bucksstar is another Starbucks knock-off in the Middle Kingdom.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;KicKer Candy Bars&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\n\"Give me a break. Break me off a piece of that KicKer bar.\" &lt;a rel=\"no follow\" href=\"http:\/\/en.rocketnews24.com\/2012\/12\/24\/obama-fried-chicken-ridiculous-knockoff-goods-from-china\/\"&gt;KicKer bars&lt;\/a&gt; are basically KitKats; they're chocolately deliciousness draped over thin, crispy wafers. Of course, the name \"KicKer\" might make the candy sound more like a punishment \u2014 or a cocktail \u2014 than a sugary treat, but, hey, why not just go with it?\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Arm and Hatchet Baking Soda&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\n&lt;a rel=\"no follow\" href=\"https:\/\/www.flickr.com\/photos\/kafka4prez\/2348899252\/sizes\/m\/\"&gt;&lt;img class=\"aligncenter size-medium wp-image-12417\" src=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/03\/Untitled4-308x410.png\" alt=\"baking soda, brand names, knock-offs, misspelling\" width=\"308\" height=\"410\" \/&gt;&lt;\/a&gt;\r\n\r\nYou can use baking soda for all sorts of things; use it to clean your house, do your laundry, or brighten up your smile. Sure, you could go with the classic Arm and Hammer baking soda, but &lt;a rel=\"no follow\" href=\"http:\/\/www.mainstreet.com\/slideshow\/funniest-product-knockoffs\/page\/3\"&gt;Arm and Hatchet&lt;\/a&gt; sounds a little more powerful, doesn't it? The products are the same, but the labels and the pictures are different. Arm and Hatchet's logo features \u2014you\u00a0guessed it\u2014a hand holding a small axe instead of a hammer.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;ABCIDS Athletic Wear&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\nAdidas is an icon in the sports world, so it makes sense that someone would try to capitalize on the brand's popularity by creating products with a similar image and font but with a different brand name. Some claim that \"ADIDAS\" is an acronym for \"All day I dream about sports.\" ABCIDS, however, well\u2026it kind of sounds like some sort of alphabet disease.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;WuMart: The Wal-Mart of China&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\nThere's no shortage of bargains in China, and you'll find plenty of good prices at &lt;a rel=\"no follow\" href=\"http:\/\/www.businessinsider.com\/22-best-knockoff-products-2009-11?op=1\"&gt;WuMart&lt;\/a&gt;. It is the same sort of business as Wal-Mart; a range of items at low prices. However, the company logos are different. WuMart has more red and they don't use a star. Their stores' signs include an English translation that calls WuMart a hypermarket, whatever that is. What does the \"Wu\" in WuMart mean? The character they use literally means \"object,\" \u00a0\"thing,\" or \"matter.\" Seems reasonable, right?\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Goojje.com \u2014 Who Needs Google, Anyway?&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\nThe only way to use Google in China is via a VPN. Naturally, the solution is to create a knock-off version of Google known as Goojje. Sure, the scope of Goojje's services don't really compare to the company that served as the inspiration behind the copy, but you have to give Goojje's creators credit for seeking to fill a consumer want.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;S&amp;M's Chocolate Candies&lt;\/b&gt;\r\n\r\nWhile this product might sound like something that belongs in \"Fifty Shades of Grey,\" S&amp;M's are actually just a knock-off of good old M&amp;M's. Hopefully they taste better than their ill-thought-out name implies. Maybe they're the perfect treat for date night!\r\n\r\n&lt;a href=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/2015\/funny-phrases-the-hair-of-the-dog\/\"&gt;Funny phrases&lt;\/a&gt; and intentional misspellings make for some of the most laughable products out there. While you might never visit a WuMart or wake up with Sunbucks coffee, it is still amusing to know that shameless imitation is around to keep the entrepreneurial spirit alive. What are some of your favorite, funny product knock-offs?","post_title":"Brand Imposters: 7 Funniest Misspelled Product Knock-Offs","post_excerpt":"","post_status":"publish","comment_status":"open","ping_status":"open","post_password":"","post_name":"brand-imposters-7-funniest-misspelled-product-knock-offs","to_ping":"","pinged":"","post_modified":"2015-06-09 07:57:07","post_modified_gmt":"2015-06-09 14:57:07","post_content_filtered":"","post_parent":0,"guid":"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/?p=12415","menu_order":0,"post_type":"post","post_mime_type":"","comment_count":"0","filter":"raw"},{"ID":14635,"post_author":"1001005","post_date":"2015-06-08 07:54:27","post_date_gmt":"2015-06-08 14:54:27","post_content":"[media]&lt;img class=\"aligncenter size-full wp-image-14751\" src=\"http:\/\/www.grammarly.com\/blog\/wp-content\/uploads\/2015\/05\/VOCABULARY-for-the-GRE.jpg\" alt=\"VOCABULARY  for the GRE\" width=\"600\" height=\"314\" \/&gt;[\/media]\r\n\r\nWhether you\u2019re studying for the GRE (Graduate Record Examinations test) or just want to improve your vocabulary, these are ten words you should learn how to use right now.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Replete:&lt;\/b&gt; filled or well-supplied with something.\r\nOur cupboard is &lt;b&gt;replete&lt;\/b&gt; with canned soup.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Harbinger:&lt;\/b&gt; A person or thing that foreshadows or foretells the coming of someone or something.\r\nSome people believe that crows are &lt;b&gt;harbingers&lt;\/b&gt; of death.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Obdurate:&lt;\/b&gt; Stubbornly persistent, generally in wrongdoing; refusing to reform or repent.\r\nShe grew increasingly &lt;b&gt;obdurate&lt;\/b&gt; during her high school years.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Reprieve:&lt;\/b&gt; To cancel or postpone the punishment of someone, especially an execution; the cancellation or postponement of a punishment.\r\nHe had resigned himself to his fate but was granted a &lt;b&gt;reprieve&lt;\/b&gt; at the last minute.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Obfuscate:&lt;\/b&gt; render obscure, unclear, or unintelligible; to bewilder someone.\r\nSometimes it\u2019s helpful to abbreviate long words. Other times, the abbreviations &lt;b&gt;obfuscate&lt;\/b&gt; the meanings of the words.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Crepuscular:&lt;\/b&gt; of, resembling, or relating to twilight.\r\nA &lt;b&gt;crepuscular &lt;\/b&gt;light filled the ballroom, creating an atmosphere of hushed anticipation.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Temper &lt;\/b&gt;(verb): To moderate or control; to strengthen or toughen a material, especially metal, by heat treatment.\r\nHe &lt;b&gt;tempered&lt;\/b&gt; his feelings in order to give a civil reply.\r\nAfter the fire had been extinguished, they discovered that the heat had &lt;b&gt;tempered &lt;\/b&gt;the metal beams.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Plumage: &lt;\/b&gt;Feathers, either covering a bird or used ornamentally; finery or elaborate dress.\r\nThe bird\u2019s &lt;b&gt;plumage&lt;\/b&gt; was exquisite: red, yellow, and orange feathers that shone like the rays of the sun.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Bolster:&lt;\/b&gt; To brace, reinforce, secure, or support.\r\nShe &lt;b&gt;bolstered&lt;\/b&gt; the team\u2019s mood with a short pep during the break.\r\n\r\n&lt;b&gt;Epicure:&lt;\/b&gt; A person who takes particular pleasure in fine food and drink.\r\nHe is an avid &lt;b&gt;epicure&lt;\/b&gt; and tries to go to the opening of every new restaurant in town.\r\n\r\nDo you have tips for learning new vocabulary words?
